< Review>
We camped in the campground with a 20' trailer. It was not easy getting up Kaiser pass with it during such a busy time of year but the destination was well worth it. The campground has multiple places to access the river for swimming and riding rapids, as well as good fishing spots. Bathrooms were well kept and despite the campground being full, we didn't feel crowded. The hot springs and Doris Lake were fun little hiking trips and towards the end of my trip I treated myself to an hour at the bathhouse in a private tub with hot mineral water from the natural springs ($7 per 30 min).<//Review>

< Text>
Not easy to get to but fun to get to. Quaint and interesting when you do get there. We stopped in at the cafe for lunch while hunting for hot springs. The cafe had great burgers and good beer. The hot springs were meh. In one of the hot springs there are creepy mud faces that previous visitors have sculpted into the banks.<//Text>

< Text>
This place is heaven on Earth! I've stayed a couple times in the campground, only for a few days on long weekends. Finally, I was able to book a cabin for a whole week and got a chance to explore the area (soak in Little Eden, swim in Tule Lake, drive to Ward Lake, rent a boat on Florence Lake, hike to Silver Pass on JMT etc). All of these places were unique and incredibly scenic. Not to mention the hot springs and the river. One day I swam 5 times and still couldn't get enough of it. This was one of the best vacations I've ever had. A badly needed break in the midst of the pandemic.
All employees were incredibly helpful and went above and beyond to ensure we had a good stay (e.g. fixed our clogged restroom and even gave us refund for it).
COVID regulations of the Fresno County were followed - people wore facemasks inside the store, showers were desinfected after each use.
Tip: Verizon doesn't have cell coverage here, only AT&T does (even LTE), consider buying a temporary prepaid sim card before going.< /Text>

< review>
Stayed in 3 of the one room housekeeping cabins, they are the cheapest option before tent cabins and we had 10 people. We got a nicely secluded and area for cabins 8, 9, 10. It is so beautifully quiet up there, really a welcome change from the busy hell that yosemite has become. The drive on kaiser pass isnt scary or dangerous, its mainly navigating the oncoming traffic, would not do it at night though!

We really enjoyed nearby doris lake and I also hiked with a friend to devil‚Äôs bathtub. Many other bountiful options are nearby in terms of hikes. I would definitely come prepared with your own food, the restaurant is what you‚Äôd expect in a place so rustic and remote, the food at the general store is marked up due to remoteness too. Best bet is to bring your own cooler and just restock ice every day. We did a lot of delicious campfire cooking and brought a propane stovetop.

My biggest gripe was with the hours of the bathhouse/spa. The only showers in the whole place are part of this facility which is only open 10am-8pm. Tough if you want to shower before or after a long hike. The natural hot springs were interesting, though not my favorite. They are in the ruins of old spas, have a lot of floating material in them. Definitely bring at least 3 kinds of bug spray, the major rains from this winter mean MANY mosquitoes.<//review>

<Text>Shortly ‚Äì it was a very good experience. Very nice, unique place.

For details, see below.

ROAD: Many people are talking here about the road, so I will tooJ. A 4x4 is NOT required to get there. Or any kind of big car is NOT required/necessary/preferred. You‚Äôll be fine on your Prius, Fusion, Focus, Corolla or whatever it is. ¬†Because of the reviews here, I took my expedition, but it‚Äôs only advantage was its size and comfort. The road is narrow and bumpy, but the bumps are not big enough to stop your vehicle of any kind. Once again, the 2 things to be aware of on the last 13 miles is the¬†narrow road¬†(just 1 way. Although, all the drivers are very polite and there are many ‚Äúturn arounds‚Äù to use, so you won‚Äôt have to back up, if there‚Äôs a car ahead of you.) and¬†sharp turns. That‚Äôs about it. If I ever decide to go there again (it is unlikely. See below why), I‚Äôll just drive my sedan.

CABINS. This place is most accurately described as a campsite. So don‚Äôt expect too much urban civilization. After all, it‚Äôs a getaway camp. BUT¬†I am taking a star off¬†for the MICE we were accompanied by at night. Fine with me, but my wife was quite scared and didn‚Äôt feel comfortable.

NATURE. Now this is what you should be coming here for. The Nature. It‚Äôs beautiful, it‚Äôs majestic, it‚Äôs breathtaking. AND this place is not very populated (at least as of now, Sept 2018). I love getaway places so this was perfect for me. Hikes towards your hot springs vs just having a pool by the hotel is super fun.

*something to be aware of: When you arrive there, they will give you a little map of the place. Well‚Ä¶ my suggestion would be not to rely too much on that mapJ)) it gives a good general understanding of what‚Äôs where, but that‚Äôs it. I.E. 2 cm on 1 portion of the map could represent 200FT and to the left of the map those same 2 cm could be actually a mile long‚Ä¶ So‚Ä¶ just keep that in mind.

Would I go there again? Once again, great place, good experience. But I drove there for 5 hrs, one way (from Sacramento) and in my opinion it is not worth it. Not their fault, of course. I would do it for 3 hrs, but not 5.<//Text>< Rate>

<Response>None< /Response><Text>I'm so torn about this place...like a lot of places actually. The location is a bit off the beaten trail and requires you to do the last 12 or 13 miles on a one lane paved road with a few areas that you're looking down a cliff side. There are cars, trucks and RVs thing both ways do it can be a bit tense at times. Apparently my wife and another camper there have PTSD from that road. The other camper actually left early because she had to get it over as soon as possible! Lol. Unbelievable!

We studied in a tent cabin that was bare bones but serviceable. There was a wooden deck, solar powered light in the tent, cots with mattresses, a picnic table and bear box. Bears came thru at night so be sure you use the box or leave your food and coolers in the car covered up!

Once you were there you are surrounded by granite features that my kids loved to climb and scramble on. The river was a great place to sit and even take a lazy ride down stream in an inner tube.

The fly fishing was so relaxing (small fingerlings) and they even stock the river in a couple of places so you can catch your meals if you want to with a spinner and lures.

There are a couple of lakes that are a bit of a hike but so worth it once you get there. Don't forget your water. You're going to need it. I would even recommend some food and swim wear do you can relax there for a couple of hours.< /Text>< Date>

<Review>Majestic. Without judgment of not knowing what it would be, other than "outdoorsy camping spot at elevation", I was blown away. We car camped the first few nights, great camp host, then got a cabin the last night. Campsites each so unique, some too close to neighbors with kids :p but breathtaking. Paved road in camp area made getting to bathroom accessible for wheelchair. Our first campsites had soft sand, not great to roll on, we moved to an area on river side who's main area was more compacted and easier to roll on. Not really great, but more possible than many other camping options. Getting to natural Hot spring not accessible, BUT there's a concrete hot tub with rails and a drop seat to get in with natural Hot spring water. An amazing masseuse offered fantastic restorative massage. (Camping with hot tub and massage? And a restaurant! Wow) We drove in a lowered handicap accessible van, and if a few pot holes were bigger we'd be in trouble. UNDERSTAND THIS, you will have to drive slow if you have a low car, no 4 wheel drive. It's a task in patience, but absolutely can be done, and it's a gorgeous drive with breathtaking views... For the passenger!  Leaving there were fire trucks responding to a fire, that were able to pass us on this crazy cliff. You'll need a drink after you get off that road, but you'll be in a hidden Paradise.< /Review>< user_name>
Colleen Harmon< /user_name>

<review>Nice hidden place. Not a EASY drive or for the inexperienced driver the road there and back is a challenging and dangerous as I have ever navigated which is many! You will need a lot of time and patience on the road as speeds are typically 5-15 mph 5mph being more the norm due to the numerous blind very narrow sharp turns. This road can seriously mess with your vehicle! There is no way to get there once the winter snow sets in as they can easily get 15 to 25 feet of snow during the winter which completely buries what actual real road there is! Because of its adventure to get there the area is usually not overly populated which is nice! Definitely a diamond in the ruff!</review>< Pictures>

<Rating>3</Rating><Text>Six miles of highway followed by 13 miles of at-times single lane road. Four-wheel drive not necessary but recommended - other vehicles may not be sturdy enough to navigate the rough road. The springs themselves are meh at best - good if you're there. Be aware that access to the springs (there are several) require navigating over single and double-beam narrow logs that have been somewhat jerry-rigged over the river - not difficult but a challenge for those with disabilities or balance problems. There is a campground plus a resort with cabins, a restaurant, a spa, massage therapy, etc.< /Text></record>

<Rate>4<//Rate>< Review>
We camped near the Mono Hot Springs Resort. The Resort itself is very rustic.  They have small cabins and tent cabins for rent. We had dinner at the restaurant, a buffalo burger with rice and salad (no potatoes that day). Since the location of this resort is so out there we weren't surprised that the fresh food delivery might not be that great. The food was overpriced but tasty after camping for the last six days. We poked our heads into the spa area, it looked like regular bathtubs with the spring water piped in. Check for a groupon if your interested in staying at the Resort. We spent most of our time in the river and hiking around the beautiful granite rocks. The nearest natural hot spring was small and crowded, but really hot! Jennifer our camp host was very nice and friendly and knew the area very well. The road was pretty rough for us but well worth the visit.</Review>

<review>Absolutely one of my favorite places I have found in this lifetime! Between soaking in a variety of hot spings with a wide range of temperatures and views, being able to eat in restaurant with great food and tables on an outdoor patio, and because this is the part of the Sierras where they never built roads across the mountains so you don't have crowds - when I go in in Mid-June or after Labor Day in September it feels like I have the whole place practically to myself!  I'm an Internet consultant and with AT&T cell phone reception and 4G Internet connection, if I don't tell my clients I'm camping at almost 7,000 ft in the Sierra High Country they'd never know!

I've come here three trips for a couple weeks each over the last two years, and can't wait to go back this summer. Spectacular 180 degree views from sunup to sundown just up the road from the hot springs makes Mono Hot Springs for me probably the place I have found the greatest peace in this live time!<//review><pics>None< /pics><resp>None<//resp>< Gmap_id>

<UserId.>113677855626977818359< /UserId.><name>Fred Rivera</name>< Time>
1534363611531<//Time>
<pictures>None</pictures><Rate>5<//Rate>< response>
None<//response>
<Text>Once you're off the main road you have to drive a 10+ mile single lane road to Mono Hot Springs (MHS). After reading about that bumpy, rocky, scary road, we rented a 4WD SUV, plus we needed more car space then what we had. You can navigate the road with other cars but it will be a challenge. If you come across other cars going the opposite direct there are many turnouts. We passed a big delivery truck and other trucks and cars, you just have to patient and road friendly. Still, it's a scary, harrowing road as there are no guard rails. One might ask just how many cars went over the side and tumbled over the cliff. While I saw cars drive it at night, I never would,as it's pitch black and there are no lights. I suggest day time driving. Key is to drive slow and be careful. Resort - Beautiful! We occupied # 4, a double space camp site. Big area, we had two tables, a fire pit and lots of room. It was quiet and comfortable, with lots of trees and shade. One minute walk to river. Toilet facilities were decent, kept clean and stocked with TP. I just wiped the seat with a disinfectant wipe before using. Jennifer, the camp host was more than pleasant and friendly. She went out of her way to answer all our questions, gave us suggestions, and offered a map while not on duty. I actually saw her doing laundry and asked a quick question and she stopped to speak to me. She is so warm and friendly. We hiked to Doris Lake, an accomplishment for me, because it was a steep hike through a path with rocks and boulders. I had to stop many times, sweated a lot. and breathed hard, but I wanted to do it to prove to myself that I could. It took one hour to walk up and 45 minutes to walk down. The payoff was a beautiful lake. We swam and had a great time. Walking down was a lot easier. Per their website they stock the river throughout the Summer so we were excited to fish for trout. We bought all new fishing poles and tackles. Sadly, we found out the river was not stocked and there were no fish. We soaked in the hot springs, hiked, swam, and had a great time! We'll definitely be back!< /Text><Gmap_id>0x8095c3ed347155dd:0x98c0c4595a5df939</Gmap_id></record>
</dataset><record>

<text>We had a blast! The resort was booked but the camp host had a few camping spots open for the days we needed. DEFINITELY not a 1 day trip! Plan on staying minimum 2 nights to do all the hot springs, mud baths and hike up to Doris Lake & Little Eden. Awesome hikes for all ages! ‚õ∫Ô∏èüòéüòÉ Yes, as u pass Hunington Lake & go up to Mono Hot Springs  it turns into a one way street. Expect bumps, pot holes, & narrow road but we're adventurous so we didn't mind. The scenery was wonderful but if ur afraid of heights good luck. We took our Prius & had no problems. If u run into other cars coming there's little side outs that u can go to or one of u will have to reverse to get to one. The restaurant was ok for us. <time>1506880946572<//time><user_id>107182026207779768974< /user_id><gmapID>0x8095c3ed347155dd:0x98c0c4595a5df939</gmapID><resp>None<//resp>< Rating>
4< /Rating>
<user_name>Star V< /user_name>< review>
We camped here for one night, unfortunately for us the cabins required at least two night minimum. It was surprisingly busy after feeling like we got lost in the backcountry - the worn single lane road was manageable though. There is running water and various hot springs nearby with one more commercialized and others you have to cross a log to get to them from camp - go slow on the log, it begins pretty sturdy but midway is when your heavy footsteps catch up with you. We ate at the restaurant which was busy and ran out of several dishes towards the end of the night.</review>

<gmapID>0x80c287c96c20dfeb:0x8b96a813dbb89ac6< /gmapID>< Review>
Subway has disappointingly skinny subs nowadays, but not submarinas.

The staff are all quite friendly, and the options are good.

I usually get a Box Lunch Special because I can eat the 4 inch sub before my lunch break is over, and it includes cookies and chips. You can get a drink with it but it costs a bit extra.

Definitely a good pick if you're looking for a good sub place.

They also offer salads and soups, but I have never tried them.<//Review>

<Rating>5</Rating>< Review>
Have grown up with this quaint and special location. Have seen many changes, however the changes also pay respect to the past as well. Especially love how the trains pass through and even stop sometimes.

The new updated Nipton doesn‚Äôt disappoint. It has been the stopping point for many many MANY years. People are always friendly.
Sadly, COVID-19 took its toll and the little town is looking for a hero. Hoping to see it open soon, bringing back the ‚Äúyesterday‚Äù and move on to tomorrow like the amazing town it truly is!<//Review>

<user_id>102063432991041065219< /user_id>< Text>
Lovely, quaint, and historical small town; unfortunately still mostly closed off (access inside the buildings like the Trading Post) to the public as of early September 2020 due to the Covid pandemic. However, you can still walk around and appreciate the frontier atmosphere and structures/artwork from the outside. Very friendly locals. Driving here is best done via Highway 95 (Searchlight, NV route).< /Text>

<Rating>5< /Rating><Text>What a pleasant sojourn! Situated on the northern edge of the Mojave National Preserve, Nipton is a quirky historical landmark, where you can grab a beer and fries, sit in the shade, and watch the trains go by. On a motorcycle or in a car, it's a short trip from southern NV. You might not intend to go to Nipton, but you'll be glad when you end up there.</Text>< Pics>

<Rate>5</Rate><text>Located just a... 15 minute drive East of Interstate 15, this little place is just plain cozy. We visited Nipton on a driving whim/ adventure day. Once we arrived, we pulled into the trading post under a tree where there was some conveniently placed picnic table. The views are breath taking and just across from the picnic tables is a little drive/ walk area to check out the what seemed like some art out in the desert.
Our next trip, we would love to try out a cabin or one of the tee pees and just enjoy the relaxing environment.

Very cool spot close to Las Vegas. It has a mart there and a bar/restaurant. They have a hotel, cabins and camping areas. They have teepees there which have beds and power, but no heating or air conditioning. There is also RV hook ups there as well. Some very nice views from there of the desert. Good place for fun and not too far a drive. They have artistic welding projects there too which is pretty cool.</review>

< user_name>

<Time>1554613261770< /Time>< gmapID>
0x80cf13581a911fa9:0xad0c70f183c95919< /gmapID>
<response>None< /response>< review>
Cute little historic town. Fairly busy pit stop for travelers to get out & stretch their legs & explore what used to be a train depot. There's a trading post that sells snacks, drinks, local raw honey, decorative candles, woven southwestern blankets, decorative glass,  souvenirs, books about the Mojave Desert, etc., & is a museum displaying old train depot items & serves as the front desk for checking into the hotel & other accommodations. There's also a cafe next to the trading post where you can purchase a glass of ice cold beer & dine/drink on the outdoor patio/deck & relax, soak up some sun & enjoy the breeze & scenic beauty of the desert & mountains & watch the freight trains pass by quite fast.. Next to the cafe is a small hotel for travelers. There's a small area near the hotel to pitch your tent if you prefer to camp for a small fee. There's a large open area out back with several large nicely furnished teepees with air condition  as well as cabins with air condition are available for travelers with reasonable nightly rates. We're told you have to book online & that they get booked pretty fast. There's a trail that takes you around the perimeter of the large open area where you can view several tall, interesting sculptures. Thoroughly enjoyed our 1 hour pit stop at Magical Nipton. Will definitely be back to stay overnight in one of the teepees,  dine outdoors at the cafe,  sit by the campfire not far from the teepee & enjoy the night sky.</review>

<Review>Cool course but not great on a hot day. Make sure you have your own quiver since there aren't any. There are multiple to hang your bow and a decent amount of shade on the south half of the course. I like that the yardage is noted at each station with game rules if you want to follow. Plenty of scenarios for all skill levels as well as a couple of places to sight in. That hike up the hill sucks if you forgot something in your car but the honor code system is nice. I like that they keep the place fairly kept for being unmanned. Portable toilets available by the storage area if you need.<//Review>< username>
